Notes Bootcamp IT Education

This is a block note summary with data, comments, tips, concepts, ideas and general information about the IT Education Bootcamp classes in Full Stack Developer, as part of Protalento Cohort 9.1 IT training process.

Classes

  • Class 1 - 5/17/2022. Introduction. What is HTML5, CSS, Web and Internet.
  • Class 2 - 5/19/2022. Discord issues. Editors, VS Code, Indentation and HTML Structure.
  • Class 3 - 5/24/2022. Extensions, elements i, em, b and strong. Lists and HTML validator.
  • Class 4 - 5/26/2022. First styles CSS.
  • Class 5 - 5/31/2022. First styles CSS. Keyboard shortcuts and Typographies. Linking CSS style to the HTML file.
  • Class 6 - 6/2/2022. Entities and colors. Ids and Classes
  • Class 7 - 6/7/2022. Child and descendant selectors. Div and span elements.
  • Class 8 - 6/9/2022. Images: JPG, PNG and SVG (vectors)
  • Class 9 - 6/14/2022. Child and descendant selectors. Div and span elements.
  • Class 10 - 6/16/2022. Semantic structural tags. Links relatives and absolutes, mailto, tel, WhatsApp. Pseudoclasses.
  • Class 11 - 6/21/2022. Fonts. Google fonts, font face and box model part 1: margin, padding, border.
  • Class 12 - 6/23/2022. Box model part 2: margin, padding, border. Reset style sheet, universal selector, max-width and min-width. CSS sibling and CSS adjacent sibling selector. Border radius.
  • Class 13 - 6/28/2022. Javascript.
  • Class 14 - 6/30/2022. Types of data, linking of javascript file within html, interactive windows, if, if else.
  • Class 15 - 7/5/2022. If, else if, if/else if, if/else if/else.
  • Class 16 - 7/7/2022. If without brackets, switch. Functions.
  • Class 17 - 7/12/2022. Scope of functions.
  • Class 18 - 7/14/2022. For, Break, continue, arrays.
  • Class 19 - 7/19/2022. Method document.getElementById, .innerHTML, .title, .href.
  • Class 20 - 7/21/2022. Events, assignment of functions and callbacks, setTimeout, setInterval, clearInterval, addEventListener.
  • Class 21 - 7/26/2022. HTML Collection, search within HTML element, the use of this.
  • Class 22 - 7/28/2022. Discussion on the request to do a JavaScript overview and the exercise number 5. Summary about searching HTML elements in the DOM (document) getElementById, getElementsByTagName. Style management from JavaScript. Adding style to a button by JavaScript for showing and hiding elements.
  • Class 23 - 8/2/2022. ClassList (add, remove, toggle), accordion, the use of hover, for this classList and addEventListener to the accordions.
  • Class 24 - 8/4/2022. Ternary operator, short circuit operators.
  • Class 25 - 8/9/2022. Forms. Basic form, label, input, attributes, search form, sub and sup tags, vertical-align, minlength, maxlength.

  • Class 27 - 8/16/2022. Measurement units em, rem, background properties, multiple backgrounds, fixed backgrounds, box-shadow, tex-shadow.
  • Class 28 - 8/18/2022. Template strings, objects, literal syntax object, properties and methods for objects, builder functions.
  • Class 29 - 8/23/2022. Examples of builder functions (builder patterns), ECMAScript6 part 1, variable declarations let and const, console.group.
  • Class 30 - 8/25/2022. ECMAScript part 2, hoisting, arrow functions, math operations, return, math object, arrow functions and object literal syntax.
  • Class 31 - 8/30/2022. BOM, DOM, refactoring, DOMContentLoaded, querySelector, querySelectorAll, createElement, appendChild insertAdjacentElement.
  • Class 32 - 9/01/2022. Overflow, advanced pseudoclasses, responsive tables with pseudoclass, display, position relative, position absolute
  • Class 33 - 9/06/2022. Position fixed, pseudoelements (::before, ::after, ::first-line, ::first-letter), attribute selector, pseudoclass not, values for parameters and for reference (primitive values and objects), new Date(),toLocaleDateString().
  • Class 34 - 9/08/2022. Debugger, Math.random(), Math.round(Math.random() * 10), HTML events, onClick callbacks, multiple callback assignation to the event click, object event, bubbling
  • Class 35 - 9/13/2022. Bubbling and capturing, addEventListener boolean value, e.stopPropagation(), advanced events 3, 4 and 5, e.target, event delegation to document, segmented event delegation, four alternatives to use .createElement, automatic behaviour events, e.preventDefault(), setTimeout, setInterval, clearInterval, customize events, document.dispatchEvent().
  • Class 36 - 9/15/2022. Form's validation, required, minlength, mmaxlength, .checkValidity(), .value, event 'input', event 'submit' .reportValidity, .setCustomValidity, CSS styles for an error validity error sign, brief summary for hsl, error sign as a background-image in an input, .closest(), .classList.add, .classList.remove, .classList.toogle(), jqueryui.com/dialog, getbootstrap/modal, .trim(), encodeURIComponent().
  • Class 37 (Alumni 38) - 9/22/2022. Regular expressions, new RegExp, object type declarative form, literal declarative form, flab 'i', method .test.
  • Class 38 (Alumni 39) - 9/27/2022. Forms validation with regular expressions, contenteditable, localstorage, focus, select.

  • Class 41 (Alumni 42) - 10/06/2022. Integrator project, the use of BEM, structure of cards, property gap, property transitions, property transform, normalize, nth-child(), object-fit.
  • Class 42 (Alumni 43) - 10/11/2022. Project integrator, main-header, main-nav, hamburger button, flex-basis, accent-color, checked, Sass, Codepen, Less, VS Code extension Live Sass Compiler.
  • Class 43 (Alumni 44) - 10/13/2022. Installation of Sass, PowerShell commands.
  • Class 44 (Alumni 45) - 10/18/2022. For and while without body, synchronic vs asynchronic code, setTimeout, AJAX 1.
  • Class 45 (Alumni 46) - 10/20/2022. AJAX, XML vs JSON, XMLHttpRequest, xhr.readyState, xhr.open, xhr.send, xhr.responseText, addEventListener, e.target.readyState, e.target.status, getResponseHeader, getAllResponseHeaders, content-header, content-type, timeout, nulish coalescing, text/plain, method .includes for texts, SPA (Single Page Application), .hash, .slice(), forEach, classList, ariaCurrent.
  • Class 46 (Alumni 48) - 10/27/2022. JSON format, CSV format, XML format, JSON.stringify(), JSON.parse(), .forEach, .join, AJAX-JSON, method XMLHttpRequest() review, contentType review, AJAX-JSON exercises 1 and 2.

AJAX-JSON, bracket notation for properties, short circuit operator, method .join(), CSS properties overflow: hidden and tex-overflow: ellipsis, JavaScript Strict Mode, no nested AJAX, nested AJAX. Callback Hell/Pyramid of Doom, promises, method .then(), resolve(), reject().
  • Class 49 (Alumni 51) - 11/08/2022. Async/await syntax, AJAX summary, Binary AJAX 1, AJAX exercise.

  • Class 51 (Alumni 53) - 11/15/2022. Operator new, introduction to backend and Node.js, history about JavaScript and Node.js, backend technologies, semantic versioning, installation of Node.js, PowerShell Commands, Node.js commands, solution stacks (LAMP, MERN, MEAN, MEVN), npm (Node Package Management), express, package.json, method createServer, nodemon, arguments req (request) and res (response), method res.writeHead(status, headers), method res.write('We can put here parts of the response'), method res.end('response's body')

  • 1:02:00 to 1:04:00: VS Code is an open code editor developed by Microsoft is heavier than other, but it is very powerfull. VS Code is not an IDE: Integrated Development Environment, but it's very useful.
  • 1:05:00 to 1:06:00: Creation of the first file in VS Code. Not to use spaces, uppercases or characters different from the english. We can have letters, numbers, underscore_ and dash -.
  • 1:06:00 to 1:08:00: Explanation why using always lowercases. For Windows two files can't have the same name in a folder, it doesn't matter the upper and lowecases. But, there are other operative systems like Linux that allows to create two files with the same name, but difference in the upper and lower cases. As Juan explains the majority or servers use with Linux OS, so it is important to always work in lowercases for avoid system errors.
  • 1:09:00 to 1:10:00: Put the extension .html.

  • 1:22:00 to 1:24:00: But de recommended structure has !Doctype HTML, the label HTML, head (information for browsers: meta, title), body
  • 1:25:00 to 1:28:00: Attributes for labels: etiqueta atributo="valor" otro-atributo="otro-valor".
  • 1:29:00 to 1:32:00: Meta Charset explanation "UTF-8 (International Character Codification). Supports almost all languages.
  • 1:33:00 to 1:37:00: The important of good indent practices: section*3>article*2>h2{encabezado}+ul>li*4>ul>li*2>a{vinvulo}. When selecting pressing Tab move content to the right. If pressing Shift + Tab move content to the left.
  • 1:38:00 to 1:39:00: Setting select indentation in VS Code. One can set 2, 3, 4 or more spaces for indentation.
  • 1:40:00 to 1:47:00: To automatize indentation you select, right click and click "Format Selection". But this in an automatic selection, and could bring into errors. Organizing indentation. Prettier is an extension for helping you in the indentation. Prolijo is having the code in order with good indentation.
  • 1:48:00 to 1:51:00: Indentation doesn't create hierarchy. It applies to the content inside a tag.

Timeline and notes Class 3

  • 00:00 to 05:00: To create files and folders in VS Code.
  • 06:00 to 15:00: To open the Live Server Extension.
  • 16:00 to 35:00: Why the use of index.html and the browser works in an automatic way to find an index.html file. Creating a lot of content with Lorem ipsum.
  • 36:00 to 57:00: Elements i (idiomatic text, can be a taxonomic expression), em (emphasis), b (bring attention) and strong (very important). There is quote, and cite labels. Looking the information in W3.org and developermozilla.org
  • 58:00 to 1:05:00: Examples of label i and em. They look all the same but have different semantic meaning.
  • 1:06:00 to 1:23:00: Examples with label b. "Locatario" example. And strong label examples, when there element is really important. Good practices with semantic labels.
  • 1:24:00 to 1:33:00: Label br stands for "brake". It is used just in specific occasions, like in a song lyrics or in poetry. It is not necessary to put the final /, like br/, that is not used anymore. It was use for making it compatible with XTML but it is not useful today.
  • 1:34:00 to 1:51:00: Creation of lists. Alt + L(ive Server) and Alt + O(pen) or Alt + C(lose). Visit MDN Reference for searching tags, attributes and other HTML topics. Also in Whatwg.org. Try to practice the basic tags but not to use list of tags, it's not just useful. Unordered lists (ul) and ordered list (ol). Ctrl + Enter goes down the cursor and generates another line. Lists examples.
  • 1:52:00 to 2:02:00: validator.w3.org. Nested lists. Indent importance and how to move the text with shift, alt and directions.
  • 2:03:00 to 2:14:00: Block elements and line elements. Block elements can contain line elements. Line elements can contain line elements. But line elements cannot contain block elements.
  • 2:15:00 to 2:16:00: ul and li are block elements.
  • 2:17:00 to 2:30:00: Attributes give information for the elements to function. Examples of attributes in paragraphs ("title" for adding titles to paragraphs), images ("src" and "alt"). We always have to use doble quote for the values of the attributes. That's like a convention or Standard. In Javascript it is used to utilize simple or single quotation and can lead to errors.
  • 2:31:00 to 2:36:00: Attributes applied to lists. Attributes for ol type "1", "a", "i", "I". Attribute value "5" for begining in 5. With value we can change the value of the li elements. We also can mix type and value in ordered lists.
  • 2:37:00 to 2:38:00: For the ul list we the attribute type and its values are deprecated.
  • 2:39:00: Syntaxis errors and importance of closing elements.
  • 2:40:00: Farewell and other recommendations.

Timeline and notes Class 5

  • 00:00 to 53:00: Greetings and questions about discord and the 1st exercise. Alumni and free domain for 6 months. Hosting and server. A hosting can have a server FTP (File Transfer Protocol), database server, web server, e-mail server. The mate thing. Wordpress and programing. Why to learn HTML5 and CSS instead of dreamweaver, Microsoft Front Page, Wordpress and editors WYSIWYG (What You See Is What You Get), those are tools for people that don't know about web development. That's the no code development. But it is not the best quality code. Worpress, Adobe Dreamweaver, Joomla.
  • 54:00 to 1:04:00: Summary about the last class: Colors. We won't usually use the name of colors. Hexademical color format: 0 to the f (16*16*16=16.777.216 million of colors) ffffff is white, 000000 is black and when I put on the same value, e.g: 4a4a4a it is grey. If a want a clear grey a go up, hence e1e1e1 is close to f, so it will be clearer. If a put on c4c4c4 it will be darker because c is a lower value. The format hwb has not yet compatibility with browser, so try not to use it. The hexadecimal format also has a alpha channel (transparency), two more digits at the final and they also go from 00 to ff
  • 1:04:00 to 1:13:00: RGB color format: Stands for Red, Green, Blue. Red is 255, 0, 0; green is 0, 255, 0; Blue is 0, 0, 255; Grey is 100, 100, 100. It also allows to use an alpha channel and it goes from 0.00 (100% transparent) to 1 (opacity 100%)
  • 1:14:00 to 1:24:00: HSL color format: Stands for Hue Saturation Luminosity (Matiz/tono, saturaci칩n y luminosidad). Hue starts in red (value 0 starts), yellow is 60, green is 120 (middle), blue is 240 (finish), violet is 290; saturation determines how up or down is the color (from 0 to 100%) and luminosity determines how clear is the color, how much light it has (from 0 dark to 100% full of light). If you change saturation you can be becoming the color into a grayer one without changing the hue of the color. It is often used when you need to put some contrast, for example with buttons, when you need to change the color while it is in hoover state. As the other you can use the alpha channel (hsla), it goes from 0.0 (100% transparent) to 1 (opacity 100%). Try to always use hsl color format.
  • 1:24:00 to 1:26:00: Can I Use is a webpage to see if new tools are deprecated. You have to think the colors and using a palette of colors.
  • 1:27:00 to 1:39:00: Typographies. Use emmet trick sheets.

Sans-serif: Without serif (e.g: Verdana, Geneva, Tahoma, Arial, Sans-serif) Those are font websafe, that means there is a hight odd the browser has it installed.     Pseudoclasses:
    1. a:link {} for unvisited sites.
    2. a:visited {} for visited sites (In general it is decided not to change colors to visited links with accesibility exceptions.
    3. a:hover {} when the cursor is over the link. Not recommended to use properties that change the size of the element while is hoovering. They usually change the color or get underline.
    4. a:focus {} change the element when it's in focus.
    5. a:active {} it is applied when one keeps the click on a link.

  • 2:36:00: The order recommended for Pseudoclasses is:
    1. a:link {}
    2. a:visited {}
    3. a:focus {}
    4. a:hover {}
    5. a:active {}

Class 10 - 6/16/2022. Semantic structural elements.

Timeline and notes Class 10

  • 00:00 to 06:00: Questions about the font and exercises.

  • 12:00 to 1:05:00: Long time ago we used div to create blocks but div has not a semantic meaning. Importance of selector specificity. The difference in the styles in a website helps to understand where begins a part and finish another. HTML5 incorporates semantic structural elements: Those are header, nav, main, footer, section and article. When the header is alone or is a body child it is understood that it is the main header and it must not be another one. Other elements can have headers. In google we can search html5 header nav layout to see examples about semantic structures elements location. The plegable property of menu is related with responsive design. It is possible to have more than a nav, but it is rare; it is recommended to put just one nav. Within main we put everything that gives sens to the page, the representative and differencial content from any webpage. Meanwhile footer closes the page, like header, when is body child or is alone it must be just one, but other semantic elements can have a footer, as articles and sections; typically contains information about the author of the section, copyright or links to related documents. The semantic structural elements are used not just for aaccesibility issues but because of search engine optimization (SEO).
  • 1:07:00 to 1:40:00: There also are sections and articles. Explanation about a section and examples. Movistar and tuenti example about the way they use to communicate with their customers. Comments about Encanto, the movie that says "casita". An article is an independent element, tells a story, they have title, develoment and an end, it can also have a header and a footer. The article element represents a complete, or self-contained, composition in a document, page, application, or site and that is in principle, independently distributable or resusable in syndication. An article could be a forum post, a magazine or newspaper article, a blog entry, a user submitted comment, an interactive widget or a gadget, or any independent item of content. Hence, they can be share by social media or WhatsApp and is understandable. Instead a section element is the most general semantic element that we have.
  • 1:41:00 to 2:06:00: An aside not necessarily goes aside the page, can bien down, or in other part, not aside the page. The element aside define content that complements the main information. HTML5 Element Flowchart. Another semantic element is: figure. Examples about when using articles, sections and other elements. Recommendations. Review how real and known websites uses semantic elements. We can't put a number in the beginning of an id. Some questions and answers about lang property. Other accesibility comments related with the semantic elements and how browsers work.
  • 2:07:00 to 2:16:00: How to select header and footer: with a class and with a child selector body > header. Adding styles to sections and articles. Use colors for guiding while styling to see better what is happening with the code.
  • 2:17:00 to 2:40:00: Using color palettes for styling a website. Coolor.com for trending color palettes.. In coolor.com we select de palette and click in "Open in the generator". There we can add more colors. When the palette is ready copy the URL and paste as a comment in the style sheet, then we take the hexadecimal number of each color and we organize it in a list with their names for better guiding. Padding should be the same in different elements, it is better to have high difference to a slight difference in properties like that. Right click and split down to dive the VS Code screen. Whe should build a website thinking that everybody can write it easily. Putting padding in main helps when margin top of h1 does not work..
  • 2:40:00 to 2:41:00 Usually we put a width of 80% in main and center main with margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto. That way the page content will ocupy 80% of the space and will be center and will adapt to the device width.

Class 11 - 05/19/2022. Fonts. Google fonts, font face and box model part 1: margin, padding, border.

Juan's notes Class 11

  • Google fonts
  • Font face
  • Box model 1

Timeline and notes Class 11

  • 00:00 to 06:00: Questions about the ideal structure in HTML5. Asking about video example in Education IT.If we can put it in the header. Juan says we can but it is not recommended.
  • 07:00 to 16:00: Accessing Google Fonts. https://fonts.google.com/. For avoiding character brokes with the accents is better to use Latin Extended. Explanations about serif and sans serif. We can customize the text, ideally with accents. In screens we use sans serif. Examples of fonts. There are variables fonts (they support a bigger amount of thickness and variations, because they have defined the possibility to increase their trace) and font with styles (each style is a distinct file). Values of 400 are normal, 700 it is bold. It is recommend 400, 400 italic, 700 and 700 italic. Testing fonts to link into the HTML5: Source Sans Pro. Juan choose the regular 400, italic 400, bold 900 and extra light 200. We just select those that we need. There are two ways to link them to our document through several link tags: link or @import. Generally we link our style.css file where are the font definitions we want to be show by browsers. But with Google Fonts we copy the code created when we chose the fonts, we add it in the HTML5 head and after we add the link to the stylesheet file. The 1st two links helps to download faster and easier the fonts from Google Fonts and the 3th one in a link to a css file with the fonts we choose. Know, within the css file we have to put the code for calling the font, as same as it shows Google Fonts; for example font-family: 'Source Sans Pro', sans-serif;
  • 17:00 to 22:00: The problem with using link is that sometimes we will need to change the font and it is necessary to update the new links in all html pages. For that reason we better use @import. That allows us to call an css file inside another css file.. We have to located in the first line of the css file, like this: @import url:('The address'). That way when we want to do a modifying in our fonts we update our @import url once in the css and that's it, we don't need to update any other links or pages.
  • 23:00 to 33:00: Hard to read font should be used just for heading, not for the content. Some questions about fast charging. Link an import fonts does not affect the web page downloading speed. Today all browsers have functionality for this, that is called Font Face. With this procedure, when the user enters the page fonts don't get installed in the computer, they just download and are used while the page is visited.
  • 34:00 to 39:00: There are other platforms related with fonts like:
    • Dafont.com: It has payed and free commercial use fonts.
    From this kind of pages we have to download the font files and unzip it in our page folder (it can have the name fonts). To incorporate the personalized fonts into our css we have to use the @font-face property. It will create the next rule:
    @font-face {
    font-family: 'My font1'
    src: url('fonts/fontName')}
    Then we can call it using the name, for this example, 'My font1' (it is recommended to put it within single quotes).
  • 40:00 to 48:00: When we established, for example, b or strong element in a paragraph the characters get bold, but it does not mean that those characters are in a font-weight: bold or 900 state. In fact, what it is really happening is that browser calculate or adapt the characters to be seen as that. But it can be similar or different to the original bold font. Hence it is important to define the different states for a font (normal, bold, italic an bold italic), so we repeat the rule @font-face as before, but linking the source (src: url) to the bold, italic and bold italic files, declaring font-weight: bold (for bold font), font-style: italic (for italic font) and font-weight: bold; font-style: italic; (for bold italic font), and keeping the same name: 'My font1'.
  • 48:00 to 1:00:00: Box model. Example: div class="box box1". Then we add styles to .box and .box1, that is something more common that putting styles directly to div. Also it is common to name the classes with double slash: box--1, according to bem, that is a modification of the original class box. For more information go over GetBem.com. When creating secuence of numbers in VS Code we select all same type of numbers with Ctrl + D and then we press Ctrl + Alt + I to increase. In addition, we have the extension random everything to create random list of countries, names, last names, citys, numbers, dates and all other kind of stuffs. It works when we have several cursors, press Ctrl + Shift + P type ramdom and appears the different options.
  • 1:00:00 to 1:03:00: Examples of properties for boxes: width (300px; 700px; 500px;). Properties like height typically get adapt to the text content inside the box.
  • 1:00:00 to 1:26:00: Padding: Important: when we add padding in a box we are increasing its size., that can be a headache when we don't take it into account. To avoid this and keep the same box size, we need to subtract in the width the same amount of padding we're adding. Then we have padding-top; padding-bottom; padding-right and padding-left. To apply padding in all directions we just declare one value for padding. For example: padding: 75px. If in this last example we assign a width: 100% the box will be bigger than the page width and will appear an horizontal scroll bar. That happens because block elements have predefine the auto value not 100%. When we use percentage for width that is related to the container size. Questions before the break. In DevTools we can select a box or element, select the width or padding and press shift arrows up or down to increase or decrease the width, or with Ctrl pressed changes 10x, with Ctrl + Shift pressed changes 100x. We can click next to the semicolon and enters an new line to create another property. Box model presentation. We can also modify the values in the DevTools box model, but it changes it with in line code. However with refresh (F5) all disappears. But, there are ways to save those changes in DevTools/Resources/Overrides/Check Enable Local Overrides. There, it allows to add a local folder that replace or overwrites the css files from the server, for that specific page we are modifying. That way we can modify any site and then reload the page with our modifications.
  • 1:27:00 to 1:33:00: Border: For applying borders we use the properties border-width, border-style (dotted, solid, double, dashed, none), and border-color (if undefined takes the color of the font, that means the color property).
  • 1:33:00 to 1:37:00: We can define in one line the different properties for border. For example: border: #acf solid 4px; (ir doesn't matter the order). As same as padding border-width increase the size of the element or box, then we have to subtract the amount of border added to the box width.
  • 1:38:00 to 1:45:00: The same way we force the width, we can force the height of an element. For example: height: 200px; if we assign less height than needed for the content, this one is going to start to overflow. We can handle that with overflow: hidden; overflow: scroll; or overflow: auto.
  • 1:45:00 to 1:48:00: For double dash and double dotted we can create another container (e.g: div) and apply a different border to it. Another possibility is to define border images. In Google search CSS border image to see examples. That way we can add frame, like pictures or paints frames. That's the major personalization of borders. https://css-tricks.com/almanac/properties/b/border-image/
  • 1:49:00 to 1:58:00: Margins separates elements. They are distances between elements. That means that they are outside the element. The distance will be determined for the biggest margin value in each element or box. That means that margins overlap, the biggest determine the distance. There are some other circumstances where this doesn't happen. If we put margin-left: 40px; the box doesn't increase its size, that's because it has predetermined width: auto. If we put margin-right: 100px; the box will have a size of 100px less. Then we have margin-top; margin-bottom; margin-right and margin-left. To apply margin in all directions we just declare one value for margin. For example: margin: 75px. As same as we do for padding.
  • 1:58:00 to 2:05:00: With those properties (width, height, margin, padding) it is important to assign a unit of measurement (px, %, cm, em), unless the value is zero. To put the block element in the right we use margin-left: auto. To put the block element in the left we use margin-right: auto. Hence, to center a block element we use margin-left and margin-right: auto. We can do that with headings, div, boxes, p and any other block element. Bear in mind that text-align is different to align the box using margin-right, margin-left: auto.
  • 2:05:00 to 2:34:00: What happens when an element inside another element has margins. First, The margins can work with negative values, but padding can't. When the elements have padding or border (even 1 or 2 px) the margins don't go out the container or box. When in a box with margin-bottom have an element that also have margin-bottom the element's margin-bottom share the margin with the box. Margin-top: auto and margin-bottom: auto doesn't work equal as margin-left and margin-right. Box model examples in educaci칩n IT website. Farewell.

  • 1:50:00 to 2:07:00: CSS adjacent sibling selectors. The adjacent sibling combinator (+) separates two selectors and matches the second element only if it immediately follows the first element, and both are children of the same parent element. For example to select all paragraphs that come immediately after any image we can type: img + p {font-weight: bold;}. Now for all elements p children of the same parent element h2 we type: h2 ~ p {}. Take into account it functions downwards not upwards.They are useful to determine a change in the style when somenthing happens, for example a new sections begins, so we want the font-family to be change or something. We can also mix this selectors with id and class selectors: #paragraph ~ h2. (We can get the prime sign ~ with Alt Gr + + or Alt + 126). Examples of border-left-style and border-top-style.
  • 2:08:00 to 2:25:00:Border radius. The border-radius CSS property rounds the corners of an element's outer border edge. You can set a single radius to make circular corners, or two radii to make elliptical corners.. Some use of flex box: display: flex; flex-wrap: wrap; gap: 20px; justify-content: center. Border radius works as padding and margin: border-radius: 20px; adds border to all corners. 5px are more recommended, we can also work with percentage, like border-radius: 5%. If border-radius: 50% I will get a circle, but because we have an square box with width: 120px; height: 120px. Also we can change any corner, one by one: border-top-left-radius: 0px; border-top-right-radius: 55px; border-bottom-right-radius: 10px; border-bottom-left-radius: 30px; these changes in borders can be applied to an image. To hide content in a box, when content overflows we use: overflow: hidden; to add border-radius in one line we use the same rule as padding but with corners instead of sides. So, border-top-left-radius is like top side and border-bottom-right-radius is bottom side. Also clockwise. Like this: border-radius: 20px 70px 10px 0; or border-radius: 20px 40px;
  • 2:26:00 to 2:32:00: We can also change the width and height of the border radius separating it by an slash (/), like this border-radius: 20px / 70px; it produces a curve in both sides of the element, like a Chavo's barrel effect. For even more rare forms we can add several values to width and heigth: border-radius: 50px 3px / 15px; Now if we want to play a little with this there are sites like 9elements Fancy Border Radius Generator.

  • 1:28:00 to 2:04:00: Truthy and falsy values: We have the possibility to transform a value into boolean. Exclamation sign denies the following expression. For example !true is false, !false is true. For example var llueve = true | console.log(llueve) returns true | console.log(!llueve) returns false. All numbers (including Infinity), except 0, 0.0, -0, -0.0 and NaN, are considered truthy. All strings, except '' (empty strings) are considered truthy. Hence for transform any value in a boolean equvalent we can use !!true (not not true). For example: !!30 returns true; !!'Hola' returns true; !!0 returns false. It is used a lot to see if what we have is true or false. For example if we code console.log(-15) returns the value -15, but if we code console.log(!!-15) tranforms the value in boolean and returns true. We can find information about truthy and falsy in MDN web docs. True and false are values, truthy and falsy are qualifying adjectives.
    • Truthy values in MDN.
    • Falsy values in MDN
  • 2:05:00 to 2:10:00 Known about truthy and falsy is very important for conditionals. Therefore true + 8 returns 9. Also we can deny the result of an operation. For example: !(2 + 2) returns false; !!(18+2) returns true; !!(18 - 18) returns false, because the operation's result is 0.

    • != not equal or distinct (it does not take into account the type of data).
    • !== estrictly not equal or estrictly distinct (it does take into account the type of data).
    Some examples of ==, ===, !=, !==. '50' == 50 returns true; '50' == '60' returns false; 50 === '50' returns false; 'hello' == 'Hello' returns false; 'heLLo'.toUpperCase() === 'HELLO' returns true.

  • 3:00 to 7:00: Use of if without curly brackets {}. It is not a good idea because the second console.log will always be shown, independently if the condition is true or not. That happens because without brackets the console takes it as console.log outside the if. So it is used just when the console.log will be just in the next line after the if. But it is not recommended.
  • 08:00 to 16:00: Template generator extension.
  • 16:00 to 27:00: Switch: The switch statement evaluates an expression, matching the expression's value to a case clause, and executes statements associated with that case, as well as statements in cases that follow the matching case. For more information about the switch statement MDN Switch. It allows us to ask for a variable end to react possible values in the variable, as an if with a lot of else if for an specific variable. For example:
    var (day) = 'sunday'
    switch (day) {
    case 'sunday':
    console.log('It is Sunday!!')
    case 'monday':
    console.log('It is Monday!!')
    case 'tuesday':
    console.log('It is Tuesday!!')
    case 'wednesday':
    console.log('It is Wednesday!!')
    case 'thursday':
    console.log('It is Thursday!!')
    case 'friday':
    console.log('It is Friday!!')
    case 'Saturday':
    console.log('It is Saturday!!')
    }
    If is Sunday system will execute code after the colon (:), that means the console.log with the sentence 'It is Sunday', but it will also show all other next cases, with their codes. In switch the expression case 'sunday' is the same as asking if 'sunday' is estrictly equal to the variable. That means that the comparison can be affected by the type of data 'string' or number. It is possible to put to cases together to execute the same action. For example:
    case 'saturday':
    case 'sunday':
    console.log('It is Weekend')
    To cut the code we can use break, with this expression we tell the system to stop executing the code. That way, if we put a break after 'wednesday' the system will finish the task abruptly and won't show Thursday, Friday and Saturday. Usually in cases like this (the week example) we will put a break after any console.log for avoiding the system to show all other days. But it is not the better way to do it. Finally in switch we can add a default expression at the end, it is like an else, and we can use it to program what's going to happen if any case is true. For example:
    default:
    console.error('Incorrect or invalid day')
    It won't be necessary to put a break after the default, but it will be necessary before the default, that means after the console.log for cases 'saturday' and 'sunday'. By convention we locate the default at the end, but in fact we can put it in any other part inside the switch and will work all the same. But in those cases it will be necessary the break. But that looks rare, and it is not used like that. Switch is less used that if, because we can't ask for greater or less than, just for estrictly equal, also we have the aspect that is continues executing the following lines. If and his derivatives are more customizable. Instead of switch are often used another design pattern that we'll talk about later in the Bootcamp.

The var total should be created in top of the JavaScript file, there it is global, behaves according to it and the code is more prolix or tidy or organized.

  • 1:08:00 to 1:13:00: While: The while statement creates a loop that executes a specified statement as long as the test condition evaluates to true. The condition is evaluated before executing the statement. In structure is like an if, you know: if (true) {console.log('Something happens')}. Hence if we replace the if the code inside the brackets will be executed forever, causing a loop. The difference with if is that before finishing we asks again for the same condition until it'll be false. So, this is an example of a typical infinite loop:
    while (true) {
    console.log('Something happens')
    }
  • 1:13:00 to 1:25:00: Opening Firefox to see how a loop causes a fast overcharge in the computer's RAM. Formerly computers crashed for this reason. So we have to stop abruptly the process in task manager (Ctrl + Alt + Delete). If the condition is false the while won't ever be executed. To avoid the infinite loop we have to, first to determine a propriate comparative operator in the condition, and secondly to use an increment or decrement operator or an assignment operator inside the while to change the value of the variable or argument, until it get higher or lower the condition, and eventually stops the while, that means the condition becomes false. Like this:
    var counter = 0 while (counter < 5) {
    console.log('Show something in the console');
    counter++
    }
    console.log will show a counting from 0 to 5. In real life this counter variable is named i. This is like an standard name. Can be related with increment, integer or index. In any case it will be always named i. So i is equals to counter. But, if the counter is inside a while anidated to another while, by convention should be named j, and if a while inside another while and another, then is called k. Also i can be like a complement for a name, like iProduct, iCourse, iStudent, iSomething.

Class 18 - 7/14/2022. For, Break, continue, arrays.

Timeline and notes Class 18.

  • 00:00 to 06:27: Asking about personal feedback.
  • 06:27 to 17:00: The use of for. The for statement creates a loop that consists of three optional expressions, enclosed in parentheses and separated by semicolons, followed by a statement (usually a block statement) to be executed in the loop. Explanation about the use of semicolon.
  • 17:00 to 18:00: Now, the use of for. First an example of while: var i = 0;
    while (i < 10) {
    console.log('A message in the console')
    i++
    }
    This message inside the while is executed 10 times in the console. For this regular use of while is design the for. The for statement contemplate th need to star something, the need to verify certain condition and the need to change the value. The part inside the brackets is customized depending on the need. So, the for solves this three needs in just one line.
  • 18:00 to 20:00: The classic for statement is for ( 1st part; 2nd part; 3th part). In the 1st part we put the initializing code, that means the code we want to be executed first even before the start of the for, that code will repeated with each iteration (In our while example, it's equivalent to var i = 0). In the 2nd part we put the condition (i < 10) and verify if is true or false. And in the 3th part we put a counter or a change in the value (i++) to allow the for to be closer to not being true. This way:
    for (var i = 0; i < 10; i++){
    console.log('A message in the console')
    }
    This way we can replace the "while" above for a shorter expression called "for".
  • 20:00 to 22:00: If we're going to create another for, like the same the variable i is already created, so we don't use the word var. "After is the same".
  • 22:00 to 23:00: Another example, decreasing 4 to 0:
    for (i = 4; i >= 0; i++) { console.log('Value of i:', i);
    }
  • 23:55 to 27:00: Now, we can let the three parts empty. Like this: for ( ; ; ) {}. It won't create an error, instead it will create an infinite loop. That's because when executing the Javascript engine check into the for and see there is nothing to initialize in the 1st part. Then, when there is nothing in the 2nd part is always evaluated as a true. So we have an infinite loop, because the condition is always true, and as there is no counter or change in the variable, that means there is no i++, it will always be true. So, we can assign of star the variable outside the for, as a global variable. Also, the i++ can be inside the brackets. But it is rare because for doing that is better to use a while. So, it will be something like this: i = 0
    for ( ; i < 5; ) {
    console.log('Value of i:' i);
    i++;
    }
    If we put anything in the 2nd part we're going to have an infinite loop.
  • 28:00 to 31:00: Break: The break statement terminates the current loop, switch, or label statement and transfers program control to the statement following the terminated statement. We can used with while, for, and switch. It is a reserved word in JavaScript to cut abruptly a repetitive structure. For example:
    var i = 0;
    while (i < 20) {
    i++;
    console.log('Value of i:', i);
    }
    This will create a display from 0 to 20
  • 32:00 to 35:00: Now, if in the example above we want something happens from 6 to 11 we can add an if with the condition i >= 6 && i <= 11. For example:
    var i = 0;
    while (i < 20) {
    i++;
    if (i >= 6 && i <= 11) {
    console.log('value of i between 6 and 11'); } console.warn('Value of i:', i);
    }
    If we put the expression "continue" (without quotes) inside the if all the if statement will be like cut and it will continue with the other numbers. The continue cut the loop and restarts again. That way the continue statement terminates execution of the statements in the current iteration of the current or labeled loop, and continues execution of the loop with the next iteration. So, the continue could be apply like this: var i = 0;
    while (i < 20) {
    i++;
    if (i >= 6 && i <= 11) {
    console.log('value of i between 6 and 11'); console.log('.'); console.log('..'); console.log('...'); continue; } console.warn('Value of i:', i);
    }
    The continue avoid the execution of the if condition, and avoid the console to show the console.warn for the values between 6 and 11. If we put the continue after console.log('.'); it won't show console.log('..'); neither console.log('...');
    The statements break and continue are the best way to solve the exercise class 17 time 1:50 to 1:54:00.

That mean, if we have if (i === 8 && confirm('Do you want to interrupt the cycle?') {break}, when i === 8 is false the JavaScript engine doesn't matter to continue analizing the next part of the &&, because in any case it will be a false result. That's why in this example JavaScript show the confirme pop-up just once. That is called a lazy expression. The break and continue should be inside an structure to have sense, like a while, for, if, or switch. Declarative functions are read by JavaScript engine as they were located on top of the file, it doesn't matter their location, that concept is called hoisting and is related with raising values to be available as they were in the top of code. JavaScript Hoisting refers to the process whereby the interpreter appears to move the declaration of functions, variables or classes to the top of their scope, prior to execution of the code. However if the variable assignment of the function is not executed yet the console.log won't work, because the variable doesn't exist.

  • 41:00 to 42:00: Ternary operator. The conditional (ternary) operator is the only JavaScript operator that takes three operands: a condition followed by a question mark (?), then an expression to execute if the condition is truthy followed by a colon (:), and finally the expression to execute if the condition is falsy. This operator is frequently used as an alternative to an if...else statement.
  • 43:00 to 50:00: Ternary is used to replace if and else with the same variable. Like this:
    1. Assign an empty variable: var message = '';
    2. Assign another: var language = 'es';
    3. Apply the conditional: if (language === 'es') {message = 'Hola!';}
    4. Add an else: else {message = 'Hello!';}
    5. console.log(message);
    The ternary in this case will create to different values to the same variable from a determined condition. So it will be like this:
    1. message = (language === 'es') ? 'Hola!' : 'Hello!';
    2. console.log(message);
    The ternary is asking if the expression in the left of the exclamation sign (?) is true assign 'Hola', else (:) assign 'Hello!'. In other word a ternary is like: variable = condition ? 'value if true' : 'value if false';
  • 51:00 to 1:22:00: Lazy loading, emphasis in the use and meaning of ternary. Another ternary example with a discount:
    1. var withDiscount = (boolean, can be true or false);
    2. var price = 200;
    3. console.log('Total: ')
    4. console.log(withDiscount ? price * 0.8 : price);
    Ternary can be use in rare and unexpected ways, it can work but is not commun use. Some other examples of rare uses of ternary. If possible not do something like this:
    1. var trueValue = 'Initial value';
    2. var falseValue = 'Initial value';
    3. Rare ternary (don't do it like this): true ? trueValue = 'A' : falseValue = 'B';
    In th assignation we don't put a new variable, we just don't do that, it's hard to understand. It 's better to use an if...else. Instead of a wear ternary like balance > 20000 ? console.log('You can buy') : console.error('Insufficient balance'); use an if...else:
    1. if (balance > 20000) {console.log('You can buy')}
    2. else {console.error('Insufficient balance');}
    It's easier to read. We can skip the brackets but it is not recommended, without the proper use of the comma, the expressions after the first one can be displayed in the console.
  • 1:23:00 to 1:28:00: An example of optimized code with jQuery, a tool to minimize code in just one line, automatically generated. Another explanation about ternary, do not use nested ternaries, it's a bad idea.
  • 1:29:00 to 1:39:00: Questions and concerns about exercise corrections or reviews. The answer, there is no time for that in classes. Discussion about discord.
  • 1:39:00 to 1:50:00: Short circuit operators: || OR examples:
    • var expression1 = 10; var expression2 = 'Hello';
    • if (expression1) is true.
    • if (expression2) is true.
    • if (2 || 8) is true, but it doesn't return a boolean, in fact it returns a 2, because it will return the first value that is true.
    • if (2 || 0 || -3 || null || undefined || '') is true and also returns 2.
    • if (0 || 0 || -3 || null || undefined || '') is true and returns -3, for the reason above.
    If I store the expression inside the condition, it won't be fulfilled with a boolean but with the first true value. So or take the first true and ignores the rest.
  • 1:50:00 to 2:11:00: Another examples of short circuit operators with OR ||:
    1. var x1;
    2. var result1 = 0 || (x1 = ('' || 2)) // generates x1 = 2 and result1 = 2 (it assigns 2 to x1, and 2 to result1)
    3. console.log('x1:', x1); // 2
    4. console.log('result1:', result1); // 2
    5. var x2;
    6. var result2 = 0 || (x2 = '') || 2 // generates x2 = '' and result2 = 2 (it assigns '' to x2, and 2 to result2)
    7. console.log('x2:', x2); // ''
    8. console.log('result2:', result2); // 2
    SyntaxError is a major error because it breaks all the code, and nothings runs, and it can happen just for a bracket or a comma.
  • 2:11:00 to 2:25:00: The AND && does the same but it returns the first falsy. && AND examples:
    • var firstFalsy1 = 15 && 'abc' && 0 && 'hola' && 15.2; it returns 0, because it's the first falsy value.
    • var firstFalsy2 = 15 && 'abc' && 4 && '' && 180; it returns '', because it's the first falsy value.
    • var firstFalsy3 = 15 && 'abc' && 4 && 57 && 180; it returns 180, the last value, because there is no falsy value.
    • If we have 5 && true && x && y; it returns an uncaught reference error saying that x is not defined, because JavaScript engine returns x, but it realizes there is no value defined for that variable and it's not created.
  • 2:26:00 to 2:36:00: Summary functions, getElementsByTagName, addEventListener, If...else, ternary and application of || and &&: Fist we create an HTML form with a button:
    • var inputNombre = document.getElementById('nombre');
    • document.getElementsByTagName('button')[0].addEventListener('click', function (){}
    • console.log('Bot칩n clickeado');
    • console.log(inputNombre);
    • var mensaje;
    • console.log(inputNombre.value);
    Then we can solve this with three different ways:
    • Con if/else: if (inputNombre.value) {mensaje = inputNombre.value;} else {mensaje = '(no asignado)';}
    • Con ternario: mensaje = inputNombre.value ? inputNombre.value : '(no asignado)';
    • Con Short-circuit operator: mensaje = inputNombre.value || '(no asignado)'; console.log(mensaje);

Class 25 - 8/9/2022. Forms. Basic form, label, input, attributes, search form, sub and sup tags, vertical-align, minlength, maxlength. Inputs for name, lastname, Email, phone, nationality, gender, address, age, select element, fieldset tag, textarea tag, button tag.

  • 00:00 to 02:00: Questions about addEventListener and event delegation.
  • 03:00 to 34:00:Basic form. HTML defines the structure and interactivity is determined by a programming language. All forms will be contained within a form tag. Input is an empty tag and it puts an space where users can add information. They're like generic boxes and they're line elements. Labels are like stickets. We can get within the label the input, but it brings problems with CSS, to give separated style to both elements. Also, we can link labels and inputs using for in label and id in input. This is useful for accesibility. Now to check if it works we click the label and automatically should be active the input. By default inputs have the attribute type: text, if we change the type by "submit" it will send information: input type="submit". The text in the input "submit" appears in the same language of the Operative System. We also have the attribute value to add an initial content within the input: input value="Ernesto". It works like a charged information than we can change after. Instead placeholder attribute is like a hint to help users what type of content they should add. Users can't change the placeholder text. Placeholder should never be used as a replacement for labels. It's a rookie mistake. Value attribute overwrites the placeholder attribute. We can change the value of the submit button with the value attribute: input type="submit" value="Send". The form is not finished until we establish an action attribute, that defines the landing page where it will be send the data, for example: form action="search.html".For the data to be organized in the landing page we have to name the inputs with the attribute name: input id="user" name="user" and input name="email" id="email" placeholder="usuario@mail.com" value="ernesto111@gmail.com". It is an important work that name does, and we have to take into account that it is name who send and organize the information in server, not ids, that's another rookie mistake. We can see how name works with the browser direction bar. Hence, when we add data to the inputs with name attributes it generates a particular direction declaring the sent data, like this: http://127.0.0.1:5501/01-basic-form/search.html ? user=eroca&emailernesto111%40gmail.com We can see there how is divided the direction by the question sign ?, so information in left is the direction where inputs are stored and information rifght is the data stored. The ampersand sign separates any new datum added. This is in fact a form created to ask for data not to post data. To define the send form we have to use the attribute method. That attribute is set by default with the value get method="get", and if we want to post then we just have to change that value: form action="search.html" method="post". It is recommended to use always English words for attributes like for, id, name. The name of the input should be the same word of the label. For example label user; input name="user", label article input name="article", if I use in this last example input name="prouct" it can create confusion. Placeholder is a new attribute of HTML. Some questions about the difference between get and post, and what's better to use input or button. Comments about validations, comments about methods or verbs get, post, put delete and others in the back-end are used as an API (Application Programming Interface).

  • 08:00 to 14:00: As was said before form tags has the method="get" by default and are use when we are searching, asking or looking for information. To upload file, to register, to log in or to publish something we have to change the form method="post".. With method="get" all the information shared to the server appears in the addres bar, however with method="post" anything appears in the address bar and creates a different error. With get all the information about the form appears in the address bar. But eventually we won't be able to send an infinite quantity of information, it's limited. The method get has a limit related with the maximum lenght for addresses determined by each browser. With get we can't send images. When we put the method post we won't see anything in the address bar, but the page will receive the information. To see more about forms and inputs visit MDN form and MDN inputs and check for methods, attributes and values, like colors, date, range.

    Celda 1 Celda 2 Celda 3
    Celda 1 Celda 2 Celda 3
    Celda 1 Celda 2 Celda 3

Class 27 - 8/9/2022. Measurement units rem and em, background properties, multiple backgrounds, fixed backgrounds, box-shadow, tex-shadow.

Timeline and notes Class 27.

  • 00:00 to 12:00: 1 rem = root element (HTML) font-size. When font-size is not defined it's, usually, 16px. Some examples: width: 50rem = width: 800px.
  • 12:00 to 25:00:1 em = 1 time the container element font-size. When font-size is not defined in the element it takes the inherited font-size from his container element. Hence if we have nested lists and we use em to the nested li elements we can generate an effect of increment or decrement of size. The container element font-size is tipically in pixels or in a fixed unit.
  • 25:00 to 27:00:Rem is simpler to use than em, but it depends on the HTML font-size, and em is interesting because if we use em in all elements everything can be proportionally changed changing the container font-size. Both are plenty use in coding at the same time.
  • 28:00 to 35:00: Regularly we use pixels when we don't what that size depends on other elements size. Pixels are good to define shadows or border-radius.
  • 36:00 to 47:00:Background properties. Element img is a semantic element brings information about somenthing specific. It's not decorative, it helps users to understand the information. If the image has a decorative purpose we should use background-image properties in CSS. Elements img has a place in the HTML code, but background-images are located backwards of the elements. For background-images we can use absolute or relative urls. So we have to take into account that the url comes from the CSS file where are calling the image, for example: background-image: url('../img/ocean.jpg'). It is recommended to use for the same box, container or element apply a background-color with a similar color to the background-image in case this one doesn't work. It's useful colorcop.
  • 48:00 to 49:00: With the property background-repeat we define if the image repeats or not: background-repeat: no-repeat; background-repeat: repeat-x; background-repeat: repeat-y; background-repeat; repeat (to repeat the image in all directions).
  • 50:00 to 1:15:00: With background-attachement we define if the image will stay fixed or if it will move with the scroll (this is the default value), so background-attachement: scroll; background-attachement: fixed. With fixed value the image is located in the top left corner of the viewport, for that reason it's important to set the property background-repeat: repeat-y with the background-attachement: fixed. Other properties are background-size: 200px; background-position: 140px 30px; the first value set the x value and the second the y value. Also with background-position we can use words like top, left, right, bottom and center: background-position: 20px bottom; background-position: bottom center. When one word is missed the default value of the next one is center. It doesn't matter the order of the words. THe property background-size also can be set with x and y values, like: background-size: 300px 70px; background-size: auto 300px; or others like background-size: contain, hence the image will be as big as the container; background-size: cover; covers all the container space with the image. Background images are located by default top left of the container, so if we change the background-position: top right and set the background-size: cover the behaviour of the image when gets smaller or bigger will be related with this new position. If we set background-size: 50%; means that the image will have a 50% width size of the container element. It's not recommended to allow an image to stretch when resized, at least we're working with textures or images that hid in a certain way the stretch defects.
  • 1:15:00 to 1:35:00: Multiple backgrounds, that means to put in one container several background images at the same time. Example son, grass, montain and clouds backgrounds to create a pretty beautiful and dinamic background for a webpage. To see more Class 27: 03 - Multiple Backgrounds

  • 1:52:00 to 2:20:00: Property box-shadow, according to MDN Web Docs adds shadow effects around an element's frame. You can set multiple effects separated by commas. A box shadow is described by X and Y offsets relative to the element, blur and spread radius, and color. Take into account shadows has no color, but for practical and graphic purpose we consider they're black. So we stablihed a black color with an alfa value transparent. Hence the third value represents the blur-radius for the shadow: /* offset-x | offset-y | blur-radius | color */ box-shadow: 10px 5px 5px rgba(0, 0, 0, .3); a fourth value determines the shadow size. Now we can apply several shadows to an box and create visual effects. An additional shadow can be more realistic. The value inset put the shadow inside the box: box-shadow: inset 10px 5px 5px rgba(0, 0, 0, .3); to create the feeling of volume in a box we can apply the following code: box-shadow: inset 4px 4px 7px rgba(0, 0, 0, .3), -1px -1px 0 rgba(0, 0, 0, .3), 1px 1px rgba(255, 255, 255, .4). They idea to make shadows is to use internet tools, like:
    • CSSGenerator.org
    • Beautiful CSS box-shadow examples
    • Box-Shadow CSS Generator
    • CSS-Tricks Box-shadow
    • MDN Box-Shadow Generator
  • 2:20:00 to 2:31:00: Property text-shadow, according to MDN text-shadow adds shadows to text. It accepts a comma-separated list of shadows to be applied to the text and any of its decorations. Each shadow is described by some combination of X and Y offsets from the element, blur radius, and color. It' almost the same as box shadow but doesn't allow to do all things we can do with box-shadow. It means is more limited and easier to work with.. Some examples for text-shadow: text-shadow: 0 0 15px yellow; text-shadow: 2px -3px 4px hsla(0, 0%, 0%, .4). For a neon effect: #neon { background-color: #000; color: #fff; font-size: 7em; padding: 2em; text-shadow: 0 0 10px #fff, 0 0 20px #fff, 0 0 30px #fff, 0 0 40px #ff00de, 0 0 70px #ff00de, 0 0 80px #ff00de, 0 0 100px #ff00de, 0 0 150px #ff00de; }. For a 80's 3D style: #texto-3d-ochentoso { font-size: 7em; color: rgba(0, 165, 255, .5); text-shadow: 8px 8px rgba(250, 0, 180, .5); }. For a fire effect with text-shadow: #fuego { padding: 3em; background-color: #000; color: #fff; font-size: 10em; text-shadow: 0 0 20px #fefcc9, 10px -10px 30px #feec85, -20px -20px 40px #ffae34, 20px -40px 50px #ec4b0c, -20px -60px 60px #cd1306, 0 -80px 70px #972516, 10px -90px 80px #451b0e ; }. Get deeply looking into Class 27: 06 - text-shadow and look at the CSS style file. With text-shadow is possible to create different and interesting effects, this CSS Generator allows us to also create a lot of different shadows for texts. The expressions webkit and moz add support for old CSS versions.

Para inscribirse tener en cuenta que Lorem ipsum dolor sit amet consectetur adipisicing elit. Exercitationem nemo, explicabo eaque esse repudiandae et!   • 40:00 to 56:00: Literal syntax object: The Object literal notation is basically an array of key:value pairs, with a colon separating the keys and values, and a comma after every key:value pair, except for the last, just like a regular array. Document, arrays, functions, window are objects. Objects are data structures formed by other data structures. Languages as Java and JavaScript are full of objects. Not all elements in JavaScript are objects, for example the primitive data, number, strings, booleans, undefined, null (with type of null is declared as an object but this is a JavaScript bug). So example of objects are: var product1 = { name: 'TV LS400 4K', price: 75000, brand: 'LG' }; var product2 = { name: 'Drone Mavic Mini 2', price: 95000, brand: 'DJI' };
  • Objects has properties and functions, we call those functions within an object "methods". Object properties examples: var newCourse = { name: 'PHP', lenght: 39, turn: '15 a 18h', logged: ['Sof칤a', 'Ver칩nica', 'Mart칤n', 'Santiago'] }; To access the properties of the object newCourse we can use the following coding expressions: console.log(`name: ${newCourse.name}`); console.log(`lenght: ${newCourse.lenght}`); console.log(`turn: ${newCourse.turn}`);

  • 1:28:00 to 1:55:00: Variable declarations let and const. When we use var we can declare a variable more than one time and console won't show us any error, that can be problematic or dangerous. Instead if we use let or const it will show a syntax error: "Uncaught SyntaxError: Identifier 'lastName' has already been declared", assuring it won't be another variable declaration. Other difference is related with the scope of the variables. Also, with const we won't be able to assign again the variable, but it will be possible to change it, but through other ways, not with a new assignation, as we did with var and as we can do with let (That's the only difference between let and const). Const are not unchangable because constant is not the same as inmutable: Constant Inmmutable. The best practice is to use always const and if it doesn't work use let. If we don't need the variable to change its value we use const and let when there is no other alternative.

For example: const IVA = 19; const ENTERPRISE_NAME = 'Martelli and Associates'.Sometimes even for objects, but inmmutable ones we also use uppercases.

That's a good thing because we have more control of the variables and it's important that they respect the scope of the block they are, frecuently when we work with variables within a block we don't want them to be available outside the block, if we want that we use global variables. If I create a variable with the same name using let or const outside and inside the block they will be two different variables because of the scope, but with var will be the same variable, for var just doesn't matter the brackets and the block. Timeline and notes Class 30.

  • 00:00 to 13:00: A little review about scope of variables. var let and const. The behaviour is the same in a conditional block: if (true) { var ifVar = 'A'; let ifLet = 'B'; const ifConst = 'C'; console.log('ifVar:', ifVar); console.log('ifLet:', ifLet); console.log('ifConst:', ifConst); }; Outside the block we only can call ifVar in a console.log(ifVar), ifLet and ifConst will show "Uncaught ReferenceError: ifLet/ifConst is not defined". It happens the same with a while or a for: for (var iVar = 0; iVar < 5; iVar++) { /* ... */ }; for (let iLet = 0; iLet < 5; iLet++) { /* ... */ }; console.log('Valor de iVar despu칠s del for:', iVar);
  • 13:00 to 18:00: The scope functions is the only scope var recognize, so they won't be available outside the function, unless we create a global variable. In this case var behaves similarly as let does.
  • 19:00 to 42:00: Hoisting. The word hoisting means to raise, to hoist, to run up, to fly. According to MDN: "JavaScript Hoisting refers to the process whereby the interpreter appears to move the declaration of functions, variables or classes to the top of their scope, prior to execution of the code." To be clear with this it's important first to know the concepts of declarative and expressive syntax. In declarative syntax we put the reserve word for each term as var, function or class, but in expressive syntax we don't as assigning a value without declare the word var, for example num = 6, or putting a function inside another element. Look at this Platzi definitions: A declarative function: when we use the reserve word function at the beginning function sayHello(name) {console.log(`Hello ${name}`);}, meanwhile a expressive function begins with the reserve word var and the anonymous function is stored in the variable var name = function(name){console.log(`Hello ${name}`);}. Hoisting only apply in the reserve words var and function, it means for expressive functions does not apply the hoisting. In other wors with declarative variables, classes or functions, we can call them before they are declare and with expressive function we have to call them after the declaration. For more info about it visit: https://platzi.com/clases/1814-basico-javascript/26295-cuando-utilizar-una-funcion-declarativa-y-una-expr/. Variables declared with let and const are also hoisted but, unlike var, are not initialized with a default value. An exception will be thrown if a variable declared with let or const is read before it is initialized. Note that it is the order in which code is executed that matters, not the order in which it is written in the source file. The code will succeed provided the line that initializes the variable is executed before any line that reads it. For more info about it, visit: https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Glossary/Hoisting. Now, take into account that var is hoisted and is available from the top or the file, but it has an undefined value. In the case of let is also hoisted, it exists, but we can't access to it, for that reason if I call the let variable before the declaration it will throw an Uncaught Reference Error: (name of variable) is not defined. The true is that let is located in de temporal dead zone (TDZ). A let or const variable is said to be in a "temporal dead zone" (TDZ) from the start of the block untiSl code execution reaches the line where the variable is declared and initialized. For more info about it, visit: https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Statements/let. If we assign a function to a variable it will behave all the same. To access a variable, class or function before the declaration is a bad practice. When creating function or arrow function is common to use const to store them, because we rarely will want to make a new assignment.
  • 43:00 to 53:00: Arrow functions. Arrow functions only work for expressive functions. First, some examples of declarative and expressive functions: // Declarative function // function adding (num1, num2) { // const total = num1 + num2; // return total; // }. // expressive anonymous function // const sumar = function (num1, num2) { // const total = num1 + num2; // return total; // }; For transforming the expressive function in an arrow function, fist we remove the word "function" and put an arrow => after the arguments (num1, num2).
  • 53:00 to 1:17:00: In those cases where we have just one value to return in a function, like this: const divide = (num1, num2) => {return num1 / num2;} it is possible to remove the brackets and the word return, likr this: const divide = (num1, num2) => num1 / num2; In a real system we can have variables with names like average, totalSells, totalJanuary, totalFebruary. Some examples of arrow functions using mathematical operations: const adding = (num1, num2) => num1 + num2; const substract = (num1, num2) => num1 - num2; const multiply = (num1, num2) => num1 / num2; const dividir = (num1, num2) => num1 / num2; const power = (num1, num2) => num1 ** num2; const square = (num) => multiply(num, num); const cube = (num) => multiply(num ** 3); In these last cases, when the function receives just one parameter, we can remove the parenthesis const square = num => num * num; const cube = num => num ** 3;. In minute 56 Juan explains how to use a group of functions to calculate a value.
  • 1:13:00 to 1:19:00: In JavaScript we have mathematical constants like the value Pi Math.PI. So we can console.log(Math.PI). We can use a function to get the Pi value const getPi = () => Math.PI; for this case we can not remove the parenthesis, because it will throw an Uncaught SyntaxError.
  • 1:20:00 to 1:42:00: console.log returns nothing. Examples of function's returnings:
    • function getNumber () {return 20;}; // returns 20
    • function getString () {return 'text';}; // returns 'text'
    • function getNull () {return null;}; // returns null
    • function getUndefined1 () {return undefined;}; // returns undefined
    • function getUndefined2 () {return;}; // returns undefined. When functions has no value declared to return, they return undefined
    • function getUndefined3 () {}; // returns undefined. When functions has no return word within, they return undefined
    • function getUndefined4 () {return console.log('Something');}; // returns undefined
    That means the operations and results within a function has no relation with the return value of the function. Alert, console.log doesn't return values, confirm return a boolean and prompt returns a string. For practical effects within an arrow function for a console.log we can remove the parenthesis and the word return and this still return undefined, like this: const getUndefined5 = () => console.log('Yellow') // returns undefined. So to get the result of a function we have to return it, otherwise it will return undefined.
  • 1:42:00 to 1:50:00: Math is a built-in object that has properties and methods for mathematical constants and functions. It's not a function object. Math works with the Number type.   • 15:00 to 30:00: Overflow is a property to manage the overflow within boxes. Overflow can happen horizontally and vertically and has the following values: overflow: visible; (default value) overflow: hidden; (hid the overflow) overflow: scroll; (shows a scroll bar always and it activates when overflow) overflow: auto; (shows the scroll bar if necessary). With overflow height use to be more struggling than width. We can also set overflow for x and for y: overflow-x: hidden; overflow-y: scroll.
  • 31:00 to 34:00: For giving style to scroll bars we can use CSS-tricks.   • 34:00 to 1:22:00 Advanced pseudoclasses. They are new pseudoclasses that allow us to select elements depending on the place they are in HTML:
    • section :first-child {color: yellow;} // Primer hijo (de cualquier tipo) dentro de section (sea o no hijo de section, pero que sea un primer hijo)
    • section > :first-child {border: 1px solid red;} // Primer hijo de section (de cualquier tipo)

    • section:first-of-type {background-color: #135;} // Primer elemento section dentro de un contenedor
    • p:last-of-type {border-right: 2em solid green;} // 칔ltimo p치rrafo dentro de un contenedor

  • 1:32:00 to 1:43:00: Advanced pseudoclasses used in tables. First some examples about styles for tables using id, class, tr > *, th, thead, tbody, #info-contries tbody tr:nth-child(odd) {background-color: grey;}
  • 1:44:00 to 1:48:00:To make responsive tables we put them inside a container with the property overflow: auto;
  • 1:49:00 to CSS property display. According to MDN: "The display CSS property sets whether an element is treated as a block or inline element and the layout used for its children, such as flow layout, grid or flex."
    • .display {display: none;}
    • .display {visibility: hidden} // To disappear the element, but it's not too used, because it keeps taking its place. Default value "visible".
    • .display-inline {display: inline;} // Change block elements into line elements.
    • .display-inline-block {display: inline-block;} // They behave as block elements, but in the same line. The can have width and height.
    • .display-block {display: block;} // Change line elements into block elements.
    We can not define a width or height to line elements (a, links), first I must change their behaviour to block or inline-block with display property. In line elements padding-top and padding-bottom don't take the place of the other elements, than means the don't open the line of a paragraph. It will be seen if it has a color. It happens the same with margin-top and margin-bottom. It works with padding and margin left and right.
  • 2:07:00 to 2:29:00: Position relative and position absolute. According to MDN: "The position CSS property sets how an element is positioned in a document. The top, right, bottom, and left properties determine the final location of positioned elements." When we talk of positioned elements we're talking about elements that hasn't the position value static (default value)
    • position: static; // Default value.
    • position: relative;
    • position: absolute;
    • position: fixed;
    • position: stiky;
    The property line-height is used to separete lines of text, in general is 16px. A trick to align a text vertically in a box is, for example the box has a height of 100px, then put the line-height equals to the box height (100px). To align horizontally text-align: center. If elements are not positioned, that means they have position: static by default, it won't work the properties: left, right, top and bottom. An element with position relative keeps is original location if we don't define any of the properties left, righ, top or bottom. Now, the elements with position: relative, the properties left, right, top and bottom are related to their own sides. So if we set left: 50px; the element will move 50px from the left side to the right, if we set right: 50px; the element will move from the right side to the left. If we define in the box bottom: 50px; the element will move 50px to top, but it keeps its original espace. Position elements are located in front of the other elements of the web page, if those are not position (or with position: static). Also, we can set negative values. The z-index is related with the deep of element in the webpage. All element has by default a z-index of 0. If we have an element with 1 value that will be in front of all others, if we have two the created last one will be in front. The z-index property only works with positioned elements. If an element with position: relative has left and right at the same time or top and bottom at the same time, left wins to right, and top wins to bottom. Also we can use z-index with value negative, z-index: -1; It's common to use z-index with high values of 1000, or 100000 for having a bigger range to work.
  • 2:29:00 to 2:40:00: Position absolute. An element with position: absolute keeps is original position but stop occupying a place and interactiong with the next elements or the container. Elements with position absolute take for reference to coordinates left, rigth, top and bottom the sides of the window or the container element, as long as the containing element is positioned. In general we use a container with position: relative for the elements to respect the container position and not being crazy in the world as elements with no order or position to follow. If we use the container with position: absolute the elements will respect the container but the container won't interact with the other elements in the webpage. In position absolute if we put: right: 0; it will be located at the right of the container, top: 0; at the top, bottom: 0; at the bottom of the container, left: 0; it's the value by default.
  • 2:40:00 to 2:42:00: Some comments about flexbox and grades, that's the most common way to position elements in the web. Farewell.
